Hello all,

Here's a few ideas (or rather variations of an idea), I hope you'll
like.  

The idea behind the logo is to achieve a bold, simple, yet elegant
look...bold, to make a statement that: yes, we are gnome women and here
to participate...simple, without the frill that is commonly
stereotypical...elegant, while being bold and simple, it's still useful
to set ourselves apart and embrace who we are, GNOME women.

Constructive comments are appreciated.
http://www.isity.net/temp/gnomewomen.png

Thanks,
Diana

I was looking at Diana's, and trying to think what I would create (if =20=

I had one tiny spark of visual skill at all), then went to M=C3=A1ir=C3=AD=
n's =20
page and there were my two ideas (done much better than I could =20
imagine them).

I like the first, because it's subtle, but we may want something more =20=

direct... and the second does that. I like it because it shows us as =20
many individual parts of the project, and if you don't have your =20
toes, you fall flat on your face, so that could be an interesting =20
message. ;)

The original idea (sorry, I've forgotten who said it), of a woman =20
martial artist, kicking the Gnome foot straight at the viewer, is =20
wonderful, but difficult to create. I tried interesting my graphics-=20
mad daughter, but couldn't tear her away from yakking with her =20
friends (online: we have to unplug her).

বুধ, 2005-07-06 -র 17:30 +0930-এ, Clytie Siddall লিখেছিলেন:
Hi all,
> 
> I like the first, because it's subtle, but we may want something more  
> direct... and the second does that. I like it because it shows us as  
> many individual parts of the project, and if you don't have your  
> toes, you fall flat on your face, so that could be an interesting  
> message. ;)
> 
I dont know if this would make much sense. In India, a feet is somehow
considered a symbol of gender-based subjugation due to various cultural
practices for eg.women were not allowed to wear shoes or were made to
sit near the foot of men etc. which somehow might lead to the second
symbol to be a bit regressive in approach. perhaps this is a mental
block on my part due to the stereotypes one is exposed to in India, but
imho, it might not go down well with the handful of ladies here in India
who are at present still fighting to find their due respect in the Linux
world. this is strictly my opinion though.
regards
Runa

www.bengalinux.org
http://blogs.randomink.org/blog/29

On 12/07/2005, at 8:30 PM, Runa Bhattacharjee wrote:

> I dont know if this would make much sense. In India, a feet is somehow
> considered a symbol of gender-based subjugation due to various =20
> cultural
> practices for eg.women were not allowed to wear shoes or were made to
> sit near the foot of men etc. which somehow might lead to the second
> symbol to be a bit regressive in approach. perhaps this is a mental
> block on my part due to the stereotypes one is exposed to in India, =20=

> but
> imho, it might not go down well with the handful of ladies here in =20
> India
> who are at present still fighting to find their due respect in the =20
> Linux
> world. this is strictly my opinion though.

No, Runa, that's a very important point. If the Gnome symbol were not =20=

already a foot, I would want to exclude it, too, but you're quite =20
right that we shouldn't _stress_ it if it's enforcing any cultural =20
stereotypes of that kind.

Why a foot? (I wonder...)

<Clytie speculates: foot fetishists in the Gnome Foundation?>

It's a pity we can't just go for a nice, big, sassy letter G with the =20=

female symbol in the cross-bar.

Logos are difficult: Gnome to me symbolizes long sessions of editing, =20=

CVS and bug-reporting: how about someone banging their head on the =20
keyboard? :D

Hi! I'm not the greatest artist or anything, but felt I could give it the
ol' college try, and came up with two possible logos. Of course, if anyone
wants to take my originals (sorry, they are in Photoshop and Illustrator, as
my Linux box decided it wanted to move on to another plain of existence) and
do what you wish with them, you are by all means given permission to do so.
My logos are hereby under the same license as the original logo that I
created mine from. ^_^ 

The first one [denoted by (R)] I created in Illustrator and then copied into
Photoshop for some 'finishing' touches. It's the standard Gnome-Text logo,
with a couple of differences:

1) The foot and text have a rainbow-ish gradient
2) The Light->Dark grey gradient has a plastic wrap on it

The second one [denoted by (F)] was created in Illustrator only. It features
your standard Gnome-Text logo, but instead of the big toe, it has a nice
daisy-like flower instead.

The images, and "source"-files, are located on my laptop, which is located
at http://dohpaz.mine.nu/gnome/. I don't really have any permanent place I
could put them right now, so if you can't get them from here, then let me
know and I'll email them to you (I don't wish to bombard the list with
1.2mb--total--of data).

- Ken

Hey YetZero,

I saw something in your logos that just caught my eye and I needed to
see if I was on to something.  I hope you don't mind but I modified what
you had sent and produced this.  The foot being the e in women just
struck me as working great with the fonts and layout.  Also I thought
taking away three of the toes looked like an abstract of a flowing
person.  Just an idea I thought might be built upon.

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Luis Villa <luis.villa@gmail.com>
Date: Jul 20, 2005 10:26 AM
Subject: [gnome-love] bug day!
To: bugsquad <gnome-bugsquad@gnome.org>, gnome-list@gnome.org, Gnome-
Love <gnome-love@gnome.org>


Woot.

It is that time of the week^Wmonth^Wyear where we gather on IRC and
take a hack at bugzilla in order to help make the next GNOME release
higher quality. It's obviously been a while since we had these
regularly (though there was a small one last week) and they are needed
:)

So, some information for those who haven't heard of our bug days:

What is this thing you call 'bug day'?
==========================

Bug day is a day we get together on IRC, find bugs, and clean bugzilla
so that developers can get more work done by focusing on bugs that
matter instead of duplicates, unconfirmable bugs, and things that
they've already closed.

Who can help at a bug day?
====================

Virtually anyone. Bug day can be for the very timid, the very quiet,
or the very persistent.

You do need:
* decent ability to read English
* a user-level knowledge of GNOME
* 30 or so minutes of the day (the first time, after that you can do it
in very small chunks.)

You don't need:
* any programming ability
* any prior experience with QA
* a deep understanding of GNOME.

On the other hand, if you do have programming ability, it's also a great
way to get involved- after a few bug days, you can figure out what needs
help in gnome quickly and apply your talents there.

What will we focus on?
================

Focus this week will be on unconfirmed bugs- reading them, marking
them NEEDINFO if needed, confirming them if they are still in a newer
release, finding duplicates, etc. Easy and fun.

Where can I get more information?
=========================

Bug days have a wiki page now:
http://live.gnome.org/Bugsquad/BugDays
_______________________________________________
gnome-love mailing list
gnome-love@gnome.org
http://mail.gnome.org/mailman/listinfo/gnome-love

Hello all,

Here's a few ideas (or rather variations of an idea), I hope you'll
like.  

The idea behind the logo is to achieve a bold, simple, yet elegant
look...bold, to make a statement that: yes, we are gnome women and here
to participate...simple, without the frill that is commonly
stereotypical...elegant, while being bold and simple, it's still useful
to set ourselves apart and embrace who we are, GNOME women.

Constructive comments are appreciated.
http://www.isity.net/temp/gnomewomen.png

Thanks,
Diana

I dont know if this would make much sense. In India, a feet is somehow
considered a symbol of gender-based subjugation due to various cultural
practices for eg.women were not allowed to wear shoes or were made to
sit near the foot of men etc. which somehow might lead to the second
symbol to be a bit regressive in approach. perhaps this is a mental
block on my part due to the stereotypes one is exposed to in India, but
imho, it might not go down well with the handful of ladies here in India
who are at present still fighting to find their due respect in the Linux
world. this is strictly my opinion though.

Hi! I'm not the greatest artist or anything, but felt I could give it the
ol' college try, and came up with two possible logos. Of course, if anyone
wants to take my originals (sorry, they are in Photoshop and Illustrator, as
my Linux box decided it wanted to move on to another plain of existence) and
do what you wish with them, you are by all means given permission to do so.
My logos are hereby under the same license as the original logo that I
created mine from. ^_^ 

The first one [denoted by (R)] I created in Illustrator and then copied into
Photoshop for some 'finishing' touches. It's the standard Gnome-Text logo,
with a couple of differences:

1) The foot and text have a rainbow-ish gradient
2) The Light->Dark grey gradient has a plastic wrap on it

The second one [denoted by (F)] was created in Illustrator only. It features
your standard Gnome-Text logo, but instead of the big toe, it has a nice
daisy-like flower instead.

The images, and "source"-files, are located on my laptop, which is located
at http://dohpaz.mine.nu/gnome/. I don't really have any permanent place I
could put them right now, so if you can't get them from here, then let me
know and I'll email them to you (I don't wish to bombard the list with
1.2mb--total--of data).

- Ken

I saw something in your logos that just caught my eye and I needed to
see if I was on to something.  I hope you don't mind but I modified what
you had sent and produced this.  The foot being the e in women just
struck me as working great with the fonts and layout.  Also I thought
taking away three of the toes looked like an abstract of a flowing

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Luis Villa <luis.villa@gmail.com>
Date: Jul 20, 2005 10:26 AM
Subject: [gnome-love] bug day!
To: bugsquad <gnome-bugsquad@gnome.org>, gnome-list@gnome.org, Gnome-
Love <gnome-love@gnome.org>


Woot.

It is that time of the week^Wmonth^Wyear where we gather on IRC and
take a hack at bugzilla in order to help make the next GNOME release
higher quality. It's obviously been a while since we had these
regularly (though there was a small one last week) and they are needed
:)

So, some information for those who haven't heard of our bug days:

What is this thing you call 'bug day'?
==========================

Bug day is a day we get together on IRC, find bugs, and clean bugzilla
so that developers can get more work done by focusing on bugs that
matter instead of duplicates, unconfirmable bugs, and things that
they've already closed.

Who can help at a bug day?
====================

Virtually anyone. Bug day can be for the very timid, the very quiet,
or the very persistent.

You do need:
* decent ability to read English
* a user-level knowledge of GNOME
* 30 or so minutes of the day (the first time, after that you can do it
in very small chunks.)

You don't need:
* any programming ability
* any prior experience with QA
* a deep understanding of GNOME.

On the other hand, if you do have programming ability, it's also a great
way to get involved- after a few bug days, you can figure out what needs
help in gnome quickly and apply your talents there.

What will we focus on?
================

Focus this week will be on unconfirmed bugs- reading them, marking
them NEEDINFO if needed, confirming them if they are still in a newer
release, finding duplicates, etc. Easy and fun.

Where can I get more information?
=========================

Bug days have a wiki page now:
http://live.gnome.org/Bugsquad/BugDays
_______________________________________________
gnome-love mailing list
gnome-love@gnome.org
http://mail.gnome.org/mailman/listinfo/gnome-love

Hello all,

Here's a few ideas (or rather variations of an idea), I hope you'll
like.  

The idea behind the logo is to achieve a bold, simple, yet elegant
look...bold, to make a statement that: yes, we are gnome women and here
to participate...simple, without the frill that is commonly
stereotypical...elegant, while being bold and simple, it's still useful
to set ourselves apart and embrace who we are, GNOME women.

Constructive comments are appreciated.
http://www.isity.net/temp/gnomewomen.png

Thanks,
Diana

বুধ, 2005-07-06 -র 17:30 +0930-এ, Clytie Siddall লিখেছিলেন:
Hi all,
> 
> I like the first, because it's subtle, but we may want something more  
> direct... and the second does that. I like it because it shows us as  
> many individual parts of the project, and if you don't have your  
> toes, you fall flat on your face, so that could be an interesting  
> message. ;)
> 
I dont know if this would make much sense. In India, a feet is somehow
considered a symbol of gender-based subjugation due to various cultural
practices for eg.women were not allowed to wear shoes or were made to
sit near the foot of men etc. which somehow might lead to the second
symbol to be a bit regressive in approach. perhaps this is a mental
block on my part due to the stereotypes one is exposed to in India, but
imho, it might not go down well with the handful of ladies here in India
who are at present still fighting to find their due respect in the Linux
world. this is strictly my opinion though.
regards
Runa

Hi! I'm not the greatest artist or anything, but felt I could give it the
ol' college try, and came up with two possible logos. Of course, if anyone
wants to take my originals (sorry, they are in Photoshop and Illustrator, as
my Linux box decided it wanted to move on to another plain of existence) and
do what you wish with them, you are by all means given permission to do so.
My logos are hereby under the same license as the original logo that I
created mine from. ^_^ 

The first one [denoted by (R)] I created in Illustrator and then copied into
Photoshop for some 'finishing' touches. It's the standard Gnome-Text logo,
with a couple of differences:

1) The foot and text have a rainbow-ish gradient
2) The Light->Dark grey gradient has a plastic wrap on it

The second one [denoted by (F)] was created in Illustrator only. It features
your standard Gnome-Text logo, but instead of the big toe, it has a nice
daisy-like flower instead.

The images, and "source"-files, are located on my laptop, which is located
at http://dohpaz.mine.nu/gnome/. I don't really have any permanent place I
could put them right now, so if you can't get them from here, then let me
know and I'll email them to you (I don't wish to bombard the list with
1.2mb--total--of data).

Hey YetZero,

I saw something in your logos that just caught my eye and I needed to
see if I was on to something.  I hope you don't mind but I modified what
you had sent and produced this.  The foot being the e in women just
struck me as working great with the fonts and layout.  Also I thought
taking away three of the toes looked like an abstract of a flowing
person.  Just an idea I thought might be built upon.

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Luis Villa <luis.villa@gmail.com>
Date: Jul 20, 2005 10:26 AM
Subject: [gnome-love] bug day!
To: bugsquad <gnome-bugsquad@gnome.org>, gnome-list@gnome.org, Gnome-
Love <gnome-love@gnome.org>


Woot.

It is that time of the week^Wmonth^Wyear where we gather on IRC and
take a hack at bugzilla in order to help make the next GNOME release
higher quality. It's obviously been a while since we had these
regularly (though there was a small one last week) and they are needed
:)

So, some information for those who haven't heard of our bug days:

What is this thing you call 'bug day'?
==========================

Bug day is a day we get together on IRC, find bugs, and clean bugzilla
so that developers can get more work done by focusing on bugs that
matter instead of duplicates, unconfirmable bugs, and things that
they've already closed.

Who can help at a bug day?
====================

Virtually anyone. Bug day can be for the very timid, the very quiet,
or the very persistent.

You do need:
* decent ability to read English
* a user-level knowledge of GNOME
* 30 or so minutes of the day (the first time, after that you can do it
in very small chunks.)

You don't need:
* any programming ability
* any prior experience with QA
* a deep understanding of GNOME.

On the other hand, if you do have programming ability, it's also a great
way to get involved- after a few bug days, you can figure out what needs
help in gnome quickly and apply your talents there.

What will we focus on?
================

Focus this week will be on unconfirmed bugs- reading them, marking
them NEEDINFO if needed, confirming them if they are still in a newer
release, finding duplicates, etc. Easy and fun.

Where can I get more information?
=========================

Bug days have a wiki page now:
http://live.gnome.org/Bugsquad/BugDays
_______________________________________________
gnome-love mailing list
gnome-love@gnome.org
http://mail.gnome.org/mailman/listinfo/gnome-love
